        <article id="post-2287" class="blog_post post-2287 post type-post status-publish format-standard hentry category-security category-spring-security tag-i18n tag-messagesource tag-messagesourceaware tag-resourcebundle tag-spring-mvc tag-spring-security">

         <div class="post-content"> 
          <header class="post-header"> 
           <h1 class="post-title entry-title">Spring Security Form based Authentication – Annotations</h1> 
          </header>
          <!-- .entry-header --> 
          <div class="entry-content"> 
           <div id="ca-pub-8323278707142241:8425728018" class="ads ads_before">
            <script async src="//pagead2.googlesyndication.com/pagead/js/adsbygoogle.js"></script> 
            <!-- jeejava-1 --> 
            <ins class="adsbygoogle" style="display:block" data-ad-client="ca-pub-8323278707142241" data-ad-slot="8425728018" data-ad-format="auto"></ins> 
            <script>
(adsbygoogle = window.adsbygoogle || []).push({});
</script>
           </div>
           <p style="text-align: justify;">In my previous tutorial, I have shown&nbsp;<a title="Spring Security Form based Authentication – XML Configuration" href="http://www.jeejava.com/spring-security-form-based-authentication-xml-configuration/" target="_blank">Spring Security Form based Authentication – XML Configuration</a> but in this tutorial I will show you annotations way to configure Spring Security with Spring MVC web application to secure pages. I will create spring mvc based web application and I will configure Spring Security to protect a page from outside access.</p> 
           <p style="text-align: justify;">Spring Security allows to you to integrate security features with JEE web application easily, it takes care about all incoming HTTP requests via servlet filter, and implements “user defined” security checking.</p> 
           <p style="text-align: justify;">In this tutorial, I will show you how to integrate Spring Security 4.2.1 with Spring MVC4 web application to secure URL access.<span id="more-2287"></span><br> For this tutorial I will create maven based web project in Eclipse.</p> 
           <p><strong>Prerequisites</strong></p> 
           <p>The following configurations are required in order to run the application</p> 
           <p>Eclipse Kepler<br> JDK 1.8<br> Tomcat 8<br> Have maven 3 installed and configured<br> Spring mvc 4 dependencies in pom.xml<br> Spring security 4 dependencies in pom.xml</p> 
           <p>Now we will see the below steps how to create a maven based project in Eclipse</p> 
           <p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Step 1.</strong> Create a maven based web project in Eclipse</p> 
           <p style="text-align: justify;">Go to <code>File -&gt; New -&gt; Other</code>. On popup window under <code>Maven</code> select <code>Maven Project</code>. Then click on Next. Select the workspace location – either default or browse the location. Click on Next. Now in next window select the row as highlighted from the below list of <code>archtypes</code> and click on Next button.</p> 
           <p><code>maven-arctype-webapp</code></p> 
           <p>Now enter the required fields (Group Id, Artifact Id) as shown below</p> 
           <p>Group Id : <code>com.roytuts</code><br> Artifact Id : <code>spring-security</code></p> 
           <p><strong>Step 2.</strong> Modify the <code>pom.xml</code> file as shown below.</p> 
           <p style="text-align: justify;">The minimal dependency artifacts required for Spring Security are <code>spring-security-web</code> and <code>spring-security-config</code>.</p> 
           <p></p> 
           <div id="crayon-59d3cf7b20521357842787" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-obsidian crayon-font-consolas crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-mouseover disable-anim wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 14px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"> 
            <div class="crayon-toolbar" data-settings=" mouseover" style="font-size: 14px !important;height: 21px !important; line-height: 21px !important;">
             <span class="crayon-title"></span> 
             <div class="crayon-tools" style="font-size: 14px !important;height: 21px !important; line-height: 21px !important;">
              <div class="crayon-button crayon-nums-button" title="Toggle Line Numbers">

                   <span class="crayon-v">build</span>
                   <span class="crayon-o">&gt;</span>
                  </div>
                  <div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-59d3cf7b20521357842787-84">
                   <span class="crayon-o">&lt;</span>
                   <span class="crayon-o">/</span>
                   <span class="crayon-v">project</span>
                   <span class="crayon-o">&gt;</span>
                  </div>
                 </div></td> 
               </tr> 
              </tbody>
             </table> 
            </div> 
           </div>
           <p></p> 
           <p style="text-align: justify;">In the above pom.xml file you notice additional plugin for <code>failOnMissingWebXml</code> configuration is required because we are going to write Java code purely based on annotations, so we will delete the <code>web.xml</code> file from WEB-INF directory.</p> 
           <p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Step 3.</strong> If you see <code>JRE System Library[J2SE-1.5]</code> then change the version by below process</p> 
           <p style="text-align: justify;">Do right-click on the project and go to <code>Build -&gt; Configure build path</code>, under Libraries tab click on <code>JRE System Library[J2SE-1.5]</code>, click on Edit button and select the appropriate jdk 1.8 from the next window. Click on Finish then Ok.</p> 
           <p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Step 4.</strong> Now when the build process finished then delete the <code>web.xml</code> file from <code>WEB-INF</code> directory. Instead we will create below two classes which are equivalent to whatever were there in web.xml file</p> 
           <p></p>

package com.roytuts.spring.mvc.config;

import org.springframework.web.servlet.support.AbstractAnnotationConfigDispatcherServletInitializer;

import com.roytuts.spring.mvc.config.WebMvcConfig;
import com.roytuts.spring.security.config.WebSecurityConfig;

public class MvcWebApplicationInitializer extends AbstractAnnotationConfigDispatcherServletInitializer {

	@Override
	protected Class&lt;?&gt;[] getRootConfigClasses() {
		return new Class[] { WebSecurityConfig.class, WebMvcConfig.class };
	}

	@Override
	protected Class&lt;?&gt;[] getServletConfigClasses() {
		return null;
	}

	@Override
	protected String[] getServletMappings() {
		return new String[] { "/" };
	}

           <p></p> 
           <p style="text-align: justify;">The above class declared Spring MVC <code>DispatcherServlet</code>, that acts as a front controller to handle incoming request and response for the URL pattern <code>"/"</code>. This is equivalent to declaring DispatcherServlet in web.xml file in my tutorial <a title="Spring Security Form based Authentication – XML Configuration" href="http://www.jeejava.com/spring-security-form-based-authentication-xml-configuration/" target="_blank">Spring Security Form based Authentication – XML Configuration</a></p> 
           <p style="text-align: justify;">I have also loaded config classes WebSecurityConfig.class and WebMvcConfic.class, that are equivalent to security.xml and controllers.xml configurations in my tutorial <a title="Spring Security Form based Authentication – XML Configuration" href="http://www.jeejava.com/spring-security-form-based-authentication-xml-configuration/" target="_blank">Spring Security Form based Authentication – XML Configuration</a></p>

           </div>
           <p>The above class is equivalent to add the filter declaration <code>DelegatingFilterProxy</code> to your web.xml file.</p> 
           <p style="text-align: justify;">This provides a hook into the Spring Security web infrastructure. <code>DelegatingFilterProxy</code> is a Spring Framework class which delegates to a filter implementation which is defined as a Spring bean in your application context. In this case, the bean is named <code>springSecurityFilterChain</code>, which is an internal infrastructure bean created by the namespace to handle web security. Note that you should not use this bean name yourself.</p> 
           <p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Step 5.</strong> Create below <code>WebSecurityConfig.java</code> that is equivalent to <code>security.xml</code> file under <code>src/main/resources</code> directory in my tutorial <a title="Spring Security Form based Authentication – XML Configuration" href="http://www.jeejava.com/spring-security-form-based-authentication-xml-configuration/" target="_blank">Spring Security Form based Authentication – XML Configuration</a></p> 
           <p></p>

            <div class="crayon-plain-wrap">
             <textarea class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 14px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
package com.roytuts.spring.security.config;

import org.springframework.beans.factory.annotation.Autowired;
import org.springframework.context.annotation.Configuration;
import org.springframework.security.config.annotation.authentication.builders.AuthenticationManagerBuilder;
import org.springframework.security.config.annotation.web.builders.HttpSecurity;
import org.springframework.security.config.annotation.web.configuration.EnableWebSecurity;
import org.springframework.security.config.annotation.web.configuration.WebSecurityConfigurerAdapter;

@Configuration
@EnableWebSecurity
public class WebSecurityConfig extends WebSecurityConfigurerAdapter {

	@Autowired
	public void configureGlobal(AuthenticationManagerBuilder auth) throws Exception {
		auth.inMemoryAuthentication().withUser("roy").password("roy").roles("ADMIN");
	}

	@Override
	protected void configure(HttpSecurity http) throws Exception {
		http// ,
				.authorizeRequests()// ,
				.antMatchers("/admin")// Ensures that request with "/admin" to
										// our application requires the user to
										// be authenticated
				.access("hasRole('ADMIN')")// Any URL that starts with
											// "/admin" will
				// be restricted to users who have the
				// role "ROLE_ADMIN",
				.and()// ,
				.formLogin()// Allows users to authenticate with form based
							// login,
				.loginPage("/login")// specifies the location of the log in
									// page,
				.loginProcessingUrl("/j_spring_security_check")// login
																// processing
																// URL,
				.defaultSuccessUrl("/admin")// default-target-url,
				.failureUrl("/login?error")// authentication-failure-url,
				.usernameParameter("username")// overrides Spring's default
												// j_username with
												// username-parameter,
				.passwordParameter("password");// overrides Spring's default
												// j_password with
												// password-parameter
	}

}</textarea>

            <div class="crayon-plain-wrap">
             <textarea class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 14px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
package com.roytuts.spring.mvc.config;

import org.springframework.context.MessageSource;
import org.springframework.context.annotation.Bean;
import org.springframework.context.annotation.ComponentScan;
import org.springframework.context.annotation.Configuration;
import org.springframework.context.annotation.PropertySource;
import org.springframework.context.support.ResourceBundleMessageSource;
import org.springframework.web.servlet.ViewResolver;
import org.springframework.web.servlet.config.annotation.EnableWebMvc;
import org.springframework.web.servlet.config.annotation.ResourceHandlerRegistry;
import org.springframework.web.servlet.config.annotation.WebMvcConfigurerAdapter;
import org.springframework.web.servlet.view.InternalResourceViewResolver;

@EnableWebMvc
@Configuration
@PropertySource(value = { "classpath:messages.properties" })
@ComponentScan(basePackages = "com.roytuts.spring.security.controllers")
public class WebMvcConfig extends WebMvcConfigurerAdapter {

	@Bean
	public ViewResolver getViewResolver() {
		InternalResourceViewResolver viewResolver = new InternalResourceViewResolver("/views/", ".jsp");
		return viewResolver;
	}

	@Override
	public void addResourceHandlers(final ResourceHandlerRegistry registry) {
		registry.addResourceHandler("/static/**").addResourceLocations("/static/");
	}

	@Bean("messageSource")
	public MessageSource messageSource() {
		ResourceBundleMessageSource messageSource = new ResourceBundleMessageSource();
		messageSource.setBasename("messages");
		messageSource.setDefaultEncoding("UTF-8");
		return messageSource;
	}

}</textarea>

           </div>
           <p></p> 
           <p style="text-align: justify;">The annotation&nbsp;<code>@EnableWebMvc</code> is equivalent to <code>&lt;mvc:annotation-driven /&gt;</code> to work with annotations in Spring MVC.</p> 
           <p style="text-align: justify;">The&nbsp;<code>addResourceHandlers()</code> acts in the similar way as <code>&lt;mvc:resources location="/static/" mapping="/static/**" /&gt;</code> to load static resources from static directory.</p> 
           <p style="text-align: justify;">The annotation&nbsp;<code>@ComponentScan</code> is equivalent to <code>&lt;context:component-scan/&gt;</code> to load all annotation-driven controllers from the given base package.</p> 
           <p>I have also declared view resolver bean and message resource for <code>i18n</code> supports.</p> 
           <p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Step 7.</strong> Create below <code>messages.properties</code> file with below content and put it under <code>src/main/resources</code> folder</p>

           <p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Step 8.</strong> Create below controller with below source</p> 
           <p></p> 
           <div id="crayon-59d3cf7b20555477361882" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-obsidian crayon-font-consolas crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-mouseover disable-anim wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 14px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">

             <span class="crayon-title"></span> 
             <div class="crayon-tools" style="font-size: 14px !important;height: 21px !important; line-height: 21px !important;">
              <div class="crayon-button crayon-nums-button" title="Toggle Line Numbers">

            <div class="crayon-info" style="min-height: 19.6px !important; line-height: 19.6px !important;"></div> 
            <div class="crayon-plain-wrap">
             <textarea class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 14px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
package com.roytuts.spring.security.controllers;

import java.util.Locale;

import javax.servlet.http.HttpServletRequest;

import org.springframework.context.MessageSource;
import org.springframework.context.MessageSourceAware;
import org.springframework.stereotype.Controller;
import org.springframework.ui.Model;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.RequestMapping;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.RequestParam;

@Controller
@RequestMapping("/")
public class SpringSecurityController implements MessageSourceAware {

	private MessageSource messageSource;

	@Override
	public void setMessageSource(MessageSource messageSource) {
		this.messageSource = messageSource;
	}

	@RequestMapping("/")
	public String defaultPage(Model model) {
		model.addAttribute("msg", "Welcome to Spring Security");
		return "index";
	}

	@RequestMapping("/login")
	public String loginPage(Model model, @RequestParam(value = "error", required = false) String error,
			@RequestParam(value = "logout", required = false) String logout) {
		if (error != null) {
			model.addAttribute("error", messageSource.getMessage("login.failure.reason", null, Locale.US));
		}
		if (logout != null) {
			model.addAttribute("msg", messageSource.getMessage("logout.msg.success", null, Locale.US));
		}
		return "login";
	}

	@RequestMapping("/logout")
	public String logoutPage(Model model, HttpServletRequest request) {
		request.getSession().invalidate();
		return "redirect:/login?logout";
	}

	@RequestMapping("/admin")
	public String adminPage(Model model) {
		model.addAttribute("title", messageSource.getMessage("page.admin.heading", null, Locale.US));
		model.addAttribute("message", messageSource.getMessage("page.admin.message", null, Locale.US));
		return "admin";
	}

}</textarea>

           <p></p> 
           <p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Step 11.</strong> Below <code>admin.jsp</code> file in <code>webapp/views</code> directory is secured and user must login before viewing the content of this file. When you try to access the <code>admin.jsp</code> file then you will automatically be redirected to the <code>login.jsp</code> file.</p>

		&lt;c:if test="${pageContext.request.userPrincipal.name != null}"&gt;
			&lt;h2&gt;
				&lt;fmt:bundle basename="messages"&gt;
					&lt;fmt:message key="welcome.msg" /&gt;
				&lt;/fmt:bundle&gt;
				: ${pageContext.request.userPrincipal.name} | &lt;a
					href="&lt;c:url value='logout'/&gt;"&gt;&lt;fmt:bundle basename="messages"&gt;
						&lt;fmt:message key="logout.text" /&gt;
					&lt;/fmt:bundle&gt;&lt;/a&gt;
			&lt;/h2&gt;
		&lt;/c:if&gt;
	&lt;/div&gt;

&lt;%@ page language="java" session="true"
	contentType="text/html; charset=ISO-8859-1" pageEncoding="ISO-8859-1"%&gt;

	&lt;div id="login-box"&gt;
		&lt;h2&gt;
			&lt;fmt:bundle basename="messages"&gt;
				&lt;fmt:message key="page.login.heading" /&gt;
			&lt;/fmt:bundle&gt;
		&lt;/h2&gt;
		&lt;c:if test="${not empty error}"&gt;
			&lt;div class="error"&gt;${error}&lt;/div&gt;
		&lt;/c:if&gt;
		&lt;c:if test="${not empty msg}"&gt;
			&lt;div class="msg"&gt;${msg}&lt;/div&gt;
		&lt;/c:if&gt;
		&lt;form name='loginForm'
			action="&lt;c:url value='j_spring_security_check' /&gt;" method='POST'&gt;
			&lt;table&gt;
				&lt;tr&gt;

						value="Submit" /&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
				&lt;/tr&gt;
			&lt;/table&gt;

				value="${_csrf.token}" /&gt;
		&lt;/form&gt;

           <p><strong>Step 13.</strong> When you deploy the application and run the application you will see different output in the browser.</p> 
           <p>When you hit the URL <code>http://localhost:8080/spring-security/</code></p> 
           <p style="text-align: justify;">The page title you should see as <code>Spring Security Basic (Annotations)</code> instead of <code>Spring Security Basic (XML)</code></p> 
           <p><a href="http://www.jeejava.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/12/spring-security-home.jpg" data-rel="lightbox-0" title=""><br> <img class="alignnone size-full wp-image-2282" title="Spring Security Form based Authentication" src="http://www.jeejava.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/12/spring-security-home.jpg" alt="spring security" width="952" height="185" srcset="http://www.jeejava.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/12/spring-security-home.jpg 952w, http://www.jeejava.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/12/spring-security-home-300x58.jpg 300w, http://www.jeejava.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/12/spring-security-home-768x149.jpg 768w" sizes="(max-width: 952px) 100vw, 952px"><br> </a></p> 
           <p>When you click on link <code>Go to Administrator page</code></p> 
           <p><a href="http://www.jeejava.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/12/spring-security-login.jpg" data-rel="lightbox-1" title=""><br> <img class="alignnone size-full wp-image-2283" title="Spring Security Form based Authentication" src="http://www.jeejava.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/12/spring-security-login.jpg" alt="spring security" width="984" height="347" srcset="http://www.jeejava.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/12/spring-security-login.jpg 984w, http://www.jeejava.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/12/spring-security-login-300x106.jpg 300w, http://www.jeejava.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/12/spring-security-login-768x271.jpg 768w" sizes="(max-width: 984px) 100vw, 984px"><br> </a></p> 
           <p>When you click on <code>Submit</code> button without giving any credentials or wrong credentials</p> 
           <p><a href="http://www.jeejava.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/12/spring-security-login-error.jpg" data-rel="lightbox-2" title=""><br> <img class="alignnone size-full wp-image-2284" title="Spring Security Form based Authentication" src="http://www.jeejava.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/12/spring-security-login-error.jpg" alt="spring security" width="971" height="414" srcset="http://www.jeejava.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/12/spring-security-login-error.jpg 971w, http://www.jeejava.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/12/spring-security-login-error-300x128.jpg 300w, http://www.jeejava.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/12/spring-security-login-error-768x327.jpg 768w" sizes="(max-width: 971px) 100vw, 971px"><br> </a></p> 
           <p>When you give username/password as <code>roy/roy</code></p> 
           <p><a href="http://www.jeejava.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/12/spring-security-admin.jpg" data-rel="lightbox-3" title=""><br> <img class="alignnone size-full wp-image-2285" title="Spring Security Form based Authentication" src="http://www.jeejava.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/12/spring-security-admin.jpg" alt="spring security" width="975" height="232" srcset="http://www.jeejava.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/12/spring-security-admin.jpg 975w, http://www.jeejava.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/12/spring-security-admin-300x71.jpg 300w, http://www.jeejava.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/12/spring-security-admin-768x183.jpg 768w" sizes="(max-width: 975px) 100vw, 975px"><br> </a></p> 
           <p>When you click on <code>Logout</code> link</p> 
           <p><a href="http://www.jeejava.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/12/spring-security-logout.jpg" data-rel="lightbox-4" title=""><br> <img class="alignnone size-full wp-image-2286" title="Spring Security Form based Authentication" src="http://www.jeejava.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/12/spring-security-logout.jpg" alt="spring security" width="968" height="415" srcset="http://www.jeejava.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/12/spring-security-logout.jpg 968w, http://www.jeejava.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/12/spring-security-logout-300x129.jpg 300w, http://www.jeejava.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/12/spring-security-logout-768x329.jpg 768w" sizes="(max-width: 968px) 100vw, 968px"><br> </a></p> 
           <p>Thanks for reading.</p>

	var dropdown = document.getElementById( "cat" );
	function onCatChange() {
		if ( dropdown.options[ dropdown.selectedIndex ].value > 0 ) {
			location.href = "http://www.jeejava.com/?cat=" + dropdown.options[ dropdown.selectedIndex ].value;
		}

	dropdown.onchange = onCatChange;
